146 act may be cited as the “Fiscal Year 2026 Budget Support Emergency Act of 2025”.
147 TITLE I. GOVERNMENT DIRECTION AND SUPPORT
148 SUBTITLE A. FOIA CLARIFICATION
149 Sec. 1001. Short title.
150 This subtitle may be cited as the “Freedom of Information Clarification Emergency
151 Amendment Act of 2025”.
152 Sec. 1002. Section 204(a) of The Freedom of Information Act of 1976, effective March
153 29, 1977 (D.C. Law 1-96; D.C. Official Code § 2-534(a)), is amended as follows:
154 (a) Paragraph (20) is amended by striking the phrase “; and” and inserting a semicolon in
155 its place.
7

156 (b) Paragraph (21) is amended by striking the period and inserting a semicolon in its
157 place.
158 (c) New paragraphs (22) and (23) are added to read as follows:
159 “(22) Information or data provided by any court, federal agency, or federally
160 established agency to the Criminal Justice Coordinating Council established by the Criminal
161 Justice Coordinating Council for the District of Columbia Establishment Act of 2001, effective
162 October 3, 2001 (D.C. Law 14-28; D.C. Official Code § 22-4232);”
163 “(23) Information or data provided by any court, federal agency, or federally
164 established agency to the District of Columbia Sentencing Commission established by the
165 Advisory Commission on Sentencing Establishment Act of 1998, effective October 16, 1998
166 (D.C. Law 12-167; D.C. Official Code § 3-101 et seq.); and”.
167 SUBTITLE B. CULTURAL AND COMMUNITY AFFAIRS
168 Sec. 1011. Short title.
169 This subtitle may be cited as the “Cultural and Community Affairs Emergency
170 Amendment Act of 2025”.
171 Sec. 1012. Cultural and community affairs grants.
172 (a) The Mayor may issue grants, in accordance with the requirements set forth in the
173 Grant Administration Act of 2013, effective December 24, 2013 (D.C. Law 20-61; D.C. Official
174 Code § 1-328.11 et seq.), to individuals and organizations that provide services to District
175 residents to support cultural affairs, community relations, and community partnerships.
176 (b) The Mayor shall provide centralized review and approval of grants issued pursuant to:
8

177 (1) Section 303(10) of the District of Columbia Latino Community Development
178 Act, effective September 29, 1976 (D.C. Law 1-86; D.C. Code § 2-1313(10));
179 (2) Section 3(10) of the Office and Commission on African Affairs Act of 2006,
180 effective June 8, 2006 (D.C Law 16-111; D.C. Official Code § 2-1392(10));
181 (3) Section 3(b)(3) of the Office on African American Affairs Establishment Act
182 of 2017, effectively February 17, 2018 (D.C. Law 22-59; D.C. Official Code § 2-1398.02(b)(3));
183 (4) Section 304(c)(9) of the Office on Asian and Pacific Islander Affairs
184 Establishment Act of 2001, effective October 3, 2001 (D.C. Law 14-28; D.C. Official Code § 2-
185 1373(c)(9));
186 (5) Sections 4(b)(11), (11A), and (12) and 4a of the Office of Gay, Lesbian,
187 Bisexual, and Transgender Affairs Act of 2006, effective April 4, 2006 (D.C. Law 16-89; D.C.
188 Official Code §§ 2-1383(b)(11), (11A), and (12), and 2-1384);
189 (6) Section 3(b)(3) of the Office on Caribbean Affairs Establishment Act of 2020,
190 effective May 6, 2020 (D.C. Law 23-87; D.C Official Code § 3-1452(b)(3));
191 (7) Section 3(b)(2)(L) of the Office on Ex-Offender Affairs and Commission on
192 Re-entry and Ex-Offender Affairs Establishment Act of 2006, effective March 8, 2007 (D.C.
193 Law 16-243; D.C. Official Code § 24-1302(b)(2)(L)); and
194 (8) Section 704(6A) of the Office of Veterans Affairs Establishment Act of 2001,
195 effective October 3, 2001 (D.C. Law 14-28; D.C. Official Code § 49-1003(6A)).
196 Sec. 1013. Section 304(c)(8) of the Office on Asian and Pacific Islander Affairs
197 Establishment Act of 2001, effective October 3, 2001 (D.C. Law 14-28; D.C. Official Code § 2-
9

198 1373(c)(8)) is amended by striking the phrase “of the Office in accordance with an act of
199 Congress” and inserting the phrase “of the Office” in its place.
200 Sec. 1014. The Commission on Fathers, Men, and Boys Establishment Act of 2014,
201 effective February 26, 2015 (D.C. Law 20-155; D.C. Official Code § 3-731 et seq.), is repealed.

204 16-243; D.C. Official Code § 24-1302), is amended as follows:
205 (a) Subsection (a) is amended by striking the phrase “is established, as a subordinate
206 Executive agency within the Public Safety and Justice cluster,” and inserting the phrase “is
207 established” in its place.
208 (b) Subsection (b)(2)(L) is amended as follows:
209 (1) The lead-in language is amended to read as follows:
210 “(L) Have the authority to establish and implement a program to support
211 the employment of returning citizens through grants to employers; provided, that:”.

213 (A) The lead-in language is amended by striking the phrase “the pilot
214 program” and inserting the phrase “the program” in its place.
215 (B) Sub-sub-subparagraph (II) is amended by striking the phrase “the pilot

233 SUBTITLE C. SURPLUS PROPERTY FUND
234 Sec. 1021. Short title.
235 This subtitle may be cited as the “Surplus Property Sales Fund Emergency Amendment
236 Act of 2025”.
237 Sec. 1022. Section 805 of the Procurement Practices Reform Act of 2010, effective
238 October 22, 2015 (D.C. Law 21-36; D.C. Official Code § 2-358.05), is amended as follows:
239 (a) Subsection (c) is amended to read as follows:
11

240 “(c) Money in the Fund shall be used to pay the operational costs of OCP.”.
241 (b) Subsection (d) is amended to read as follows:
242 “(d) Any money remaining available in the Fund at the end of a fiscal year, as determined
243 by the Chief Financial Officer in the fiscal year-end close, shall be transferred to the unassigned
244 fund balance of the General Fund of the District of Columbia as part of the fiscal year-end
245 close.”.
246 SUBTITLE D. RECREATIONAL FACILITIES ASSESSMENT
247 Sec. 1031. Short title.
248 This subtitle may be cited as the “Recreational Facilities Assessment Emergency
249 Amendment Act of 2025”.
250 Sec. 1032. The Department of General Services Establishment Act of 2011, effective
251 September 14, 2011 (D.C. Law 19-21; D.C. Official Code § 10-551.01 et. seq.), is amended by
252 adding a new section 1028i to read as follows:
253 “Sec. 1028i. Recreational facilities assessment.
254 “(a) The Department shall conduct an annual survey to update information on the
255 condition of spray parks, artificial turf fields, playgrounds, and courts such as tennis, pickleball,
256 basketball, or other similar hard surface courts, as determined by the Department, at recreational
257 facilities. The survey results shall be disaggregated by facility, made publicly available, and
258 transmitted to the Council, the Council chairpersons with oversight jurisdiction over the
259 Department and the Department of Parks and Recreation, and the Office of the City
260 Administrator by March 1 of each year.
12

261 “(b) For the purposes of this section, the term “recreation facility” shall have the same
262 meaning as set forth in section 1028c(a)(2).”.
263 SUBTITLE E. HUMAN SERVICES GRANT ADMINISTRATION
264 Sec. 1041. Short title.
265 This subtitle may be cited as the “Human Services Grant Administration Emergency
266 Amendment Act of 2025”.
267 Sec. 1042. The Grant Administration Act of 2013, effective December 24, 2013 (D.C.
268 Law 20-61; D.C. Official Code § 1-328.11 et seq.), is amended by adding a new section 1099 to
269 read as follows:
270 “Sec. 1099. (a) For grants, the grant agreements for which are received by the
271 Department of Human Services (“DHS”) signed by the grantee after October 1, 2026, that are
272 funded exclusively by local operating funds, and for which DHS is the sole grantor (“DHS local
273 grants”), the first payment to the grantee under the grant shall issue no later than 30 days
274 following the start of the fiscal year or other term of service during which the grantee must
275 perform under its grant agreement with DHS or no later than 30 days following the actual receipt
276 by DHS of a signed grant agreement, whichever is later.
277 “(b) DHS shall provide the grant agreement for each DHS local grant to the grantee for
278 the grantee’s review and signature no later than 30 days following the start of the fiscal year or
279 other term of service during which the grantee must perform under its grant agreement with
280 DHS.”.
281 SUBTITLE F. ANC FUNDING FLEXIBILITY CLARIFICATION
13

282 Sec. 1051. Short title.
283 This subtitle may be cited as the “Advisory Neighborhood Commissions Funding
284 Flexibility Clarification Emergency Amendment Act of 2025”.
285 Sec. 1052. Section 16 of the Advisory Neighborhood Commissions Act of 1975, effective
286 March 26, 1976 (D.C. Law 1-58; D.C. Official Code § 1-309.13), is amended as follows:
287 (a) Subsection (b)(1) is amended as follows:
288 (1) The existing text is redesignated as subparagraph (A).
289 (2) A new subparagraph (B) is added to read as follows:
290 “(B) Every such commercial bank, savings and loan association, credit
291 union, or combination thereof, shall provide to the Office of the Chief Financial Officer at
292 oft.bankingservices@dc.gov, on a monthly or quarterly basis, depending on the frequency with
293 which each such financial institution issues such records in the ordinary course of business, a
294 copy of the account statement of each Commission for which it serves as a depository of all
295 funds received, or online access to same.”.
296 (b) Subsection (d)(1) is amended by striking the phrase “to the Council” and inserting the
297 phrase “to the Council and the OANC” in its place.
298 (c) Subsection (f)(2A)(C) is repealed.
299 (d) A new subsection (f-1) is added to read as follows:
300 “(f-1) A record or signature by an officer of a Commission who has authority to
301 sign on behalf of the Commission may be in electronic form.”.
302 (e) Subsection (h) is repealed.
14

303 (f) Subsection (l)(3) is repealed.
304 (g) Subsection (l-1)(3)(B)(i) is amended by striking the phrase “Authority;” and
305 inserting the phrase “Authority, and expenses for transportation by the use of a taxicab or
306 rideshare vehicle;” in its place.
307 (h) A new subsection (m-1) is added to read as follows:
308 “(m-1) Any services funded by a direct expenditure from a Commission must not be
309 duplicative of any services that are already performed by the District government.”.
310 (i) Subsection (q) is amended by striking the phrase “may seek to reprogram” and
311 inserting the phrase “shall provide” in its place.
312 SUBTITLE G. COMMUNITY LEGAL EDUCATION AND RESOURCES GRANT
313 PROGRAM
314 Sec. 1061. Short title.
315 This subtitle may be cited as the “Community Legal Education and Resources Grant
316 Emergency Act of 2025”.
317 Sec. 1062. (a) There is established a Community Legal Education and Resources Grant
318 Program (“Program”) to be administered by the Mayor to provide grants, pursuant to the Grant
319 Administration Act of 2013, effective December 24, 2013 (D.C. Law 20-61; D.C. Official Code §
320 1-328.11 et seq.), to legal services providers to deliver legal services.
321 (b) The Mayor, pursuant to the District of Columbia Administrative Procedure Act,
322 approved October 21, 1968 (82 Stat. 1204; D.C. Official Code Section § 2-501 et seq.), may
323 issue rules to implement the Program, including rules governing the:
15

324 (1) Types of legal services projects eligible for grant funding;
325 (2) Application process and timing; and
326 (3) Monitoring of Program performance and reporting requirements.
327 (c) For the purposes of this subtitle, the term:
328 (1) “Legal services” means:
329 (A) Legal representation of District residents, including through the
330 provision of legal advice, brief services, and limited-scope representation; or
331 (B) Training of attorneys in legal issues.
332 (2) “Legal services provider” means:
333 (A) A nonprofit organization;
334 (B) A private entity that partners with a nonprofit organization; or
335 (C) A private entity utilizing pro bono legal assistance.
336 SUBTITLE H. ACCOUNTABILITY FOR BUDGET DELAYS
337 Sec. 1071. Short title.
338 This subtitle may be cited as the “Accountability for Delaying the Budget Emergency
339 Amendment Act of 2025”.
340 Sec. 1072. If the Mayor submits an annual budget later than the date established by the
341 Council pursuant to section 442(a) of the District of Columbia Home Rule Act, approved
342 December 24, 1973 (87 Stat. 798; D.C. Official Code § 1-204.42(a)), nonpersonnel services
343 spending shall be prohibited within the Executive Office of the Mayor and the Office of the City
16

344 Administrator until the day after the date on which the Mayor submits the annual budget to the
345 Council.
346 Sec. 1073. Section 47-363(b)(3) of the District of Columbia Official Code is amended by
347 striking the phrase “is on recess.” and inserting the phrase “is on recess. If the Mayor submits an
348 annual budget later than the date established by the Council pursuant to § 1-204.42(a), no request
349 may be submitted to the Chairman of the Council under this subsection until after the date on
350 which the Mayor submits the annual budget to the Council.” in its place.
351 Sec. 1074. Section 711 of the Rules of Organization and Procedure for the Council of the
352 District of Columbia, Council Period 26, Resolution of 2025, effective January 2, 2025 (Res. 26-
353 1; 72 DCR 1289), is amended to read as follows:
354 “711. EFFECT OF RECESS AND BUDGET SUBMISSION DELAY ON
355 PROCEDURES.
356 “(a)(1) Reprogramming requests and grant budget modification requests may not be
357 submitted to the Council during a recess of the Council. No time period provided in this part for
358 the consideration of the requests will continue to run during a recess of the Council.
359 “(2) If the Mayor submits an annual budget later than the date established by the
360 Council pursuant to section 442(a) of the District of Columbia Home Rule Act, approved
361 December 24, 1973 (87 Stat. 798; D.C. Official Code § 1-204.42(a)), reprogramming requests
362 and grant budget modification requests may not be submitted to the Council until after the date
363 on which the Mayor submits the annual budget to the Council.”.

390 SUBTITLE C. NEIGHBORHOOD PROSPERITY FUND
391 Sec. 2021. Short title.
392 This subtitle may be cited as the “Neighborhood Prosperity Fund Emergency
393 Amendment Act of 2025”.
394 Sec. 2022. Section 2012(b)(3) of the Neighborhood Prosperity Initiative Act of 2018,
395 effective October 30, 2018 (D.C. Law 22-168; D.C. Official Code § 2-1210.71(b)), is amended
396 to read as follows:
397 “(3) “Qualifying project” means a mixed-use or retail real estate development
398 project that is located in a:
19

399 “(A) Low-income community, as that term is defined in section 45D(e) of
400 the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, approved December 21, 2000 (114 Stat. 2763; 26 U.S.C. §
401 45D(e));

502 SUBTITLE F. RFK CAMPUS INFRASTRUCTURE FUND
503 Sec. 2051. Short title.
504 This subtitle may be cited as the “RFK Campus Infrastructure Fund Establishment
505 Emergency Act of 2025”.
506 Sec. 2052. RFK Campus Infrastructure Fund.
507 (a) There is established as a special fund the RFK Campus Infrastructure Fund, which
508 shall be administered by the Mayor pursuant to subsections (c), (d), and (e) of this section.
509 (b) After all principal and interest on the bonds issued pursuant to section 103 of the
510 Ballpark Omnibus Financing and Revenue Act of 2004, effective April 8, 2005 (D.C. Law 15-
511 320; D.C. Official Code § 10-1601.03), has been paid, all receipts from the sports facilities fee
512 imposed by D.C. Official Code § 47-2762 shall be deposited into the RFK Campus Infrastructure
513 Fund.
514 (c) Money in the RFK Campus Infrastructure Fund shall be used:
515 (1) To pay the debt service, including principal and interest, costs of issuance, and
516 credit enhancements, and any costs of defeasance on bonds issued for RFK campus infrastructure
517 and parking facilities, and making any other payments related to such bonds;
518 (2) To fund reserves for bonds issued for RFK campus infrastructure and parking
519 facilities; and
520 (3) For the purposes set forth in and in accordance with subsection (d) of this
521 section.
25

522 (d) Any money available in the RFK Campus Infrastructure Fund in excess of the
523 amounts required to be paid or reserved pursuant to subsection (c)(1) and (2) of this section, as
524 determined by the Chief Financial Officer, shall:
525 (1) In Fiscal Years 2026 and 2027:
526 (A) Be used to pay the debt service on any ballpark early redemption
527 borrowing; and
528 (B) To the extent all debt service on any ballpark early redemption
529 borrowing has been paid, be transferred to the General Fund of the District of Columbia;
530 (2) In Fiscal Years 2028 and 2029, be transferred to the General Fund of the
531 District of Columbia;
532 (3)(A) In Fiscal Year 2030 and each fiscal year thereafter, be transferred to the
533 RFK Transportation Improvement Fund, established in the Robert F. Kennedy Campus
534 Redevelopment Act of 2025, as introduced on June 20, 2025 (Bill 26-288);
535 (B) If the amount of an annual deposit to the RFK Transportation Fund
536 pursuant to subparagraph (A) of this paragraph would exceed $20 million, $20 million shall be
537 deposited in the RFK Transportation Fund and the amount over $20 million shall be deposited in
538 the General Fund of the District of Columbia.
539 (e) The Mayor, or any District instrumentality or authority designated by the Mayor, may
540 pledge and create a security interest in the funds in the RFK Campus Infrastructure Fund for the
541 payment of the debt service on any bonds issued for RFK campus infrastructure and parking
542 facilities, any fees and charges incurred in connection therewith, and any payments owing under
26

543 any document or instrument entered into in connection with such indebtedness in accordance
544 with the provisions of the documents entered into by the District in connection with the issuance
545 of such bonds.
546 (f)(1) Except as provided in subsection (d)(3)(B) of this section, the money deposited into
547 the RFK Campus Infrastructure Fund shall not revert to the unrestricted fund balance of the
548 General Fund of the District of Columbia at the end of a fiscal year, or at any other time.
549 (2) Subject to authorization in an approved budget and financial plan, any funds
550 appropriated in the RFK Campus Infrastructure Fund shall be continually available without
551 regard to fiscal year limitation.
552 (g) For the purposes of this section, the term “RFK campus” means the parcels of land
553 that are the subject of the Transfer of Jurisdiction Plat recorded in the Surveyor’s Office of the
554 District of Columbia on February 5, 2025, on page 13 of subdivision book 223, together with any
555 public streets within or adjacent to such parcels that may be closed from time to time.

694 location other than the licensed establishment where the numbers are called by a live caller.

991 SUBTITLE L. TRUXTON CIRCLE EMINENT DOMAIN AUTHORITY
992 Sec. 2111. Short title.
993 This subtitle may be cited as the “Truxton Circle Eminent Domain Authority Emergency
994 Act of 2025”.
995 Sec. 2112. The Council finds that:
48

996 (1) The Truxton Circle neighborhood is a mixed-use neighborhood characterized
997 by mixed-density residential, commercial, and retail uses. It is a high-priority corridor for
998 investment, in-fill development, and the revitalization of vacant and underutilized lots.
999 (2) Lot 48 in Square 3100 (“the Property”), located at approximately 1600 North
1000 Capitol Street, NW, is approximately 18,984 square feet, located at the northwest intersection of
1001 North Capitol Street, NW, and Florida Avenue, NW. It is bounded by North Capitol Street, NW,
1002 to the east, Q Street, NW, to the south, and Florida Avenue, NW, to the west.
1003 (3) The property is at the intersection of two major District corridors and
1004 development of these areas is a high-priority measure for the District and residents of Ward 5.
1005 (4) The property presents the opportunity for redevelopment along North Capitol
1006 Street, NW, and a reduction in blight. This parcel is ripe for matter-of-right, neighborhood-
1007 appropriate development, including housing, retail, mixed-use development, and office space.
1008 (5) Acquisition of the property by the District will allow for development to
1009 invigorate a vacant and underutilized parcel and to reposition the property for development and
1010 revitalization.
1011 Sec. 2113. The Mayor may exercise eminent domain in accordance with the procedures
1012 set forth in Subchapter II of Chapter 13 of Title 16 of the District of Columbia Official Code to
1013 acquire Lot 48 in Square 3100 for the purpose of revitalization or redevelopment.

1043 SUBTITLE N. ROCK CREEK TENNIS CENTER TRANSFER OF
1044 JURSISDICTION
1045 Sec. 2131. Short title.
1046 This subtitle may be cited as the “Rock Creek Tennis Center Transfer of Jurisdiction and
1047 Funding Emergency Act of 2025”.
1048 Sec. 2132. (a) Pursuant to section 404 of the District of Columbia Home Rule Act,
1049 approved December 24, 1973 (87 Stat. 803; D.C. Official Code § 1-204.04), and consistent with
1050 section 1 of An Act To authorize the transfer of public land in the District of Columbia, approved
1051 May 20, 1932 (47 Stat. 161; D.C. Official Code § 10-111), the Council of the District of
1052 Columbia authorizes the transfer of jurisdiction from the Director of the National Park Service,
1053 acting on behalf of the Secretary of the Interior, to the government of the District of Columbia,
1054 over a portion of U.S. Reservation 339, which is National Park Service Land and appurtenant
1055 facilities in Rock Creek Park, the boundaries of which are generally Kennedy Place, NW, to the
1056 north; 16th Street, NW, and Colorado Avenue, NW, to the east; the inside boundary of the
51

1057 existing parking lots to the south and west; Stage Road, NW, to the west; and a portion of
1058 Morrow Drive, NW, to the existing tree line to where it intersects with Kennedy Place, NW, to
1059 the west, upon which is situated the Rock Creek Tennis Center and appurtenant facilities, as
1060 shown on a plat to be drawn and filed in the Office of the Surveyor of the District of Columbia.
1061 (b) Upon the transfer of jurisdiction described in subsection (a) of this section, or another
1062 transfer of jurisdiction approved by the Council pursuant to section 1 of An Act To authorize the
1063 transfer of jurisdiction over public land in the District of Columbia, approved May 20, 1932 (47
1064 Stat. 161; D.C. Official Code § 10-111), over the property in which the Rock Creek Tennis
1065 Center is situated, the Department of Parks and Recreation shall commence the Rock Creek
1066 Tennis Center capital project to make improvements necessary to bring the existing tennis center
1067 into compliance with Association of Tennis Professionals Tour and Women’s Tennis
1068 Association Tour event standards.
1069 Sec. 2133. It is the sense of the Council that the Mayor, in accepting a transfer of
1070 jurisdiction that includes the Rock Creek Tennis Center, should:
1071 (a) Thoroughly and thoughtfully engage with the communities and organizations
1072 impacted by the current and future uses of the property over which jurisdiction is to be
1073 transferred, including Advisory Neighborhood Commission 4E, the Rock Creek Conservancy,
1074 and residents of the Sixteenth Street Heights and Crestwood neighborhoods.
1075 (b) Provide a reasonable period of time for public comment, including opportunities for
1076 Executive agencies to answer public questions about the transfer of jurisdiction.
52

1077 (c) Incorporate any relevant environmental, traffic, and noise impact studies previously
1078 completed pertaining to the property over which jurisdiction is to be transferred, or conduct
1079 additional studies of comparable rigor and scope that should be made available to the public.
1080 (d) Prioritize preservation of open and free access to as much of the property over which
1081 jurisdiction is to be transferred as possible for as much of the year as possible, including the
1082 existing Picnic Grove #24 and public parking spaces to be utilized for public access of other
1083 areas of Rock Creek Park.
1084 (e) Explore the role of the Carter Barron Amphitheater in a proposed or future transfer of
1085 jurisdiction to ensure preservation, improvement, and future productive public use of this historic
1086 community asset.
1087 SUBTITLE O. HISTORIC BURIAL GROUNDS PRESERVATION PROGRAM
1088 Sec. 2141. Short title.
1089 This subtitle may be cited as the “Historic Burial Grounds Preservation Program
1090 Emergency Amendment Act of 2025”.
1091 Sec. 2142. The Historic Landmark and Historic District Protection Act of 1978, effective
1092 March 3, 1979 (D.C. Law 2-144; D.C. Official Code § 6-1101 et seq.), is amended by adding a
1093 new section 11c to read as follows:
1094 “Sec. 11c. Paul E. Sluby, Sr. Historic Burial Grounds Preservation Program.
1095 “(a) There is established a Paul E. Sluby, Sr. Historic Burial Grounds Preservation
1096 Program at the Office of Planning (“Office”).
53

1097 “(b) Subject to available funding, the Office shall issue grants to qualified charitable
1098 organizations for the following purposes:
1099 (1) The preservation and restoration of historic burial grounds;
1100 (2) The identification of historic burial grounds;
1101 (3) The interpretation of historic burial grounds;
1102 (4) The repatriation of human remains, particularly those from former historic
1103 burial grounds; or
1104 (5) Related research and documentation of historic burial grounds including burial
1105 records, locational data, and contested ownership.
1106 “(c) Qualified charitable organizations that seek a grant for activities at a historic burial
1107 ground that is located on private property shall be considered for a grant only with the written
1108 consent of the property owner.
1109 “(d) For the purposes of this section, the term:
1110 “(1) “Historic burial ground” means a cemetery or any natural or prepared
1111 physical location, whether originally below, on, or above the surface of the earth, into which
1112 human remains are deposited as a part of the death rite or ceremony of a culture, and that was
1113 established in the District of Columbia prior to January 1, 1955, for interments of African
1114 Americans and is owned by a public body or qualified charitable organization.
1115 “(2) “Qualified charitable organization” means a charitable corporation, charitable
1116 association, or charitable trust that has been granted tax-exempt status under § 501(c)(3) of the
1117 Internal Revenue Code and that has the primary purpose of preserving historical cemeteries and
54

1118 graves or was formed for the purpose of identifying, preserving, or maintaining historic burial
1119 grounds.”.

1215 Blossom Festival (“Program”), which shall be administered by the Washington Convention and
1216 Sports Authority (“Events DC”). Under the Program, a matching grant shall be awarded to a
1217 nonprofit organization that organizes and produces an event or events as part of the official,
1218 month-long National Cherry Blossom Festival (“Festival”) at a rate of $2 for every dollar that the
1219 organization has raised in corporate donations by April 30, 2026; except, that the total matching
59

1220 grant shall not exceed $1.5 million.
1221 (b) In Fiscal Year 2026, of the funds allocated to the Non-Departmental Account, $1.5
1222 million shall be transferred to Events DC to use for the grant authorized by subsection (a) of this
1223 section.
1224 (c) A grant awarded pursuant to this section shall be in addition to any other grant
1225 awarded by Events DC in support of the Festival.
1226 Sec. 2173. DC History Grants.
1227 (a) In Fiscal Year 2026, Events DC shall issue a grant of no less than $350,000 for the
1228 purpose of providing funds to a nonprofit organization located in the District that
1229 provides education about how the District of Columbia has been the home for the fight for
1230 freedom and democracy, with an emphasis on including the entire District across all 8 wards in
1231 this history.
1232 (b)(1) In Fiscal Year 2026, Events DC shall issue a grant of no less than $250,000 to a
1233 nonprofit organization occupying space in the Carnegie Library building that is engaged in
1234 collecting, interpreting, and sharing the history of the District.
1235 (2) A grant awarded pursuant to this subsection shall be in addition to any other
1236 grant awarded by Events DC in support of historical education and research.

1351 SUBTITLE E. BACKGROUND CHECK AND RAP BACK PROGRAM
1352 Sec. 3041. Short title.
1353 This subtitle may be cited as the “Background Check Fingerprinting Authority and Rap
1354 Back Program Emergency Act of 2025”.
1355 Sec. 3042. Definitions.
1356 For the purposes of this subtitle, the term:
1357 (1) “Covered individual” means an individual who has submitted to a fingerprint-
1358 based background check as a condition of caring for children, persons with a disability, the
1359 elderly, or vulnerable adults, a security officer, special police officer, private detective, private
1360 detective agency, security agency, or other person responsible for protecting property, preventing
1361 theft, damage to real or personal property, assaults, disorder, or other illegal occurrences, or for
1362 purposes of licensure, appointment, commission, certification, registration, employment, or
1363 volunteer service with a participating agency pursuant to District law or regulation.
1364 (2) “FBI” means the Federal Bureau of Investigation.
66

1365 (3) “FBI Rap Back Service” means the FBI Next Generation Identification
1366 Record of Arrest and Prosecution Background Service.
1367 (4) “MPD” means the Metropolitan Police Department.
1368 (5) “Notification event” means an event, such as an arrest or other criminal
1369 activity when fingerprints are taken, that triggers a notification from the FBI Rap Back Service to
1370 the Metropolitan Police Department regarding a covered individual who has been subscribed to
1371 the FBI Rap Back Service.
1372 (6) “Participating agency” means a District government agency that requires a
1373 fingerprint-based background check and receives the results as a condition of caring for children,
1374 persons with a disability, the elderly, vulnerable adults, a security officer, special police officer,
1375 private detective, private detective agency, security agency, or other person responsible for
1376 protecting property, preventing theft, damage to real or personal property, assaults, disorder, or
1377 similar illegal occurrences, or for purposes of licensure, appointment, commission, certification,
1378 registration, employment, or volunteer service.
1379 Sec. 3043. Background check fingerprinting authority.
1380 (a) If the fingerprinting of an individual is required or authorized by any District or
1381 federal law or regulation for the purposes of conducting a background check of the individual,
1382 MPD, or an entity authorized by MPD, may fingerprint the individual, forward the fingerprints to
1383 the FBI for the purpose of conducting a criminal history check, receive the results of the criminal
1384 history check, and disseminate the results of the criminal history check to entities authorized to
1385 receive the results.
67

1386 (b) The authority provided by this section applies to fingerprinting authorized under the
1387 District of Columbia Rap Back Program and to fingerprinting required or authorized by any
1388 other District or federal law or regulation.
1389 Sec. 3044. District of Columbia Rap Back Program.
1390 (a) MPD shall participate on behalf of the District in the FBI Rap Back Service, through
1391 the establishment of a District of Columbia Rap Back Program.
1392 (b) The purpose of the District of Columbia Rap Back Program shall be to allow
1393 participating agencies, through the District of Columbia Rap Back Program, to subscribe covered
1394 individuals in the FBI Rap Back Service and to be notified when a covered individual is the
1395 subject of an FBI Rap Back Service notification event.
1396 (c) If a participating agency requests that the District of Columbia Rap Back Program
1397 subscribe a covered individual in the FBI Rap Back Service, the covered individual shall be
1398 fingerprinted by MPD or an entity authorized by MPD and the fingerprints shall be forwarded by
1399 MPD to the FBI for a national criminal history check and subscription in the FBI Rap Back
1400 Service.
1401 (d) MPD shall notify the relevant participating agency when a covered individual
1402 subscribed by the participating agency in the FBI Rap Back Service through the District of
1403 Columbia Rap Back Program is the subject of an FBI Rap Back Service notification event.
1404 (e) For the purposes of administering the District of Columbia Rap Back Program and
1405 performing or facilitating criminal history background screenings, MPD is authorized to take the
1406 fingerprints of a covered individual, submit to the FBI the fingerprints of, and accompanying
68

1407 records regarding, a covered individual, and allow such fingerprints and records to be retained by
1408 the FBI Rap Back Service and used for ongoing searches through the FBI Rap Back Service.
1409 Sec. 3045. Limitation on use of information.
1410 The information contained in a notification event received by a participating agency shall
1411 be used by the participating agency only for the purpose of determining a covered individual’s
1412 eligibility to care for children, persons with a disability, the elderly, or vulnerable adults, a
1413 security officer, special police officer, private detective, private detective agency, security
1414 agency, or other person responsible for protecting property, preventing theft, damage to real or
1415 personal property, assaults, disorders, or similar illegal occurrences, or for purposes of licensure,
1416 appointment, commission, certification, registration, employment, or volunteer service and shall
1417 not be further disseminated by the participating agency.
1418 Sec. 3046. Fees.
1419 MPD may establish by rule a fee, to be imposed on a covered individual or participating
1420 agency, for subscription of a covered individual in the District of Columbia Rap Back
1421 Program. The fee may be imposed on an annual basis.
1422 Sec. 3047. Rules.
1423 MPD may issue rules, pursuant to Title I of the District of Columbia Administrative
1424 Procedure Act, approved October 21, 1968 (82 Stat. 1204; D.C. Official Code § 2-501 et seq.), to
1425 govern the implementation of the District of Columbia Rap Back Program and to otherwise
1426 implement the provisions of this subtitle.

1866 “Sec. 203c. Dual-language program feasibility study.
1867 “(a) By January 1, 2026, the Deputy Mayor for Education (“DME”) shall complete a
1868 feasibility study for the development and operation of a new dual-language education program or
1869 dual-language education school, located in Ward 6, 7, or 8 and serving grades 6 through 8.
1870 “(b) The study shall:
1871 “(1) Consider the feasibility of:
1872 “(A) Using the Winston Education Campus as a site for a dual-language
1873 education program or a school that hosts a dual-language education program;
1874 “(B) Embedding a dual-language education program into an existing
1875 middle school in Ward 6, 7, or 8, including Kelly Miller Middle School, Kramer Middle School,
1876 Sousa Middle School, and Jefferson Academy Middle School;
1877 “(C) Utilizing the Shirley Chisholm Elementary School modernization to
1878 establish a dual-language education campus at Shirley Chisholm Elementary School; and
1879 “(D) Incorporating Ward 6, 7, and 8 dual-language education public
1880 charter school elementary schools without an existing or nearby middle school feeder into a
1881 DCPS dual-language education program or middle school feeder pattern;
99

1882 “(2) Assess the feasibility of each option in paragraph (1) of this subsection based
1883 on the following considerations:
1884 “(A) Capital and operational costs;
1885 “(B) Staffing requirements and models;
1886 “(C) The transportation time of the students and families likely to attend
1887 the new school or program;
1888 “(D) The impact on enrollment patterns of the elementary and middle
1889 schools in the proposed or existing feeder patterns; and
1890 “(E) Enrollment trends of English learners, by in-boundary and out-of-
1891 boundary status, to attend such a dual-language program or school;
1892 “(3) Analyze the demand in Wards 7 and 8 for a dual-language education middle-
1893 grade option, which shall include:
1894 “(A) The number of students living in Wards 7 and 8 who attend a dual-
1895 language elementary school in the District outside of those wards; and
1896 “(B) The number of families living in Wards 7 and 8 waitlisted at dual-
1897 language elementary schools in the District outside of those wards over the last 5 school years;
1898 and
1899 “(4) Propose timelines for implementing the 3 most feasible options for a dual-
1900 language education program or school located in Ward 6, 7, or 8, serving grades 6 through 8.
1901 “(c) “Dual-language education” means a course of study where students study grade-level
1902 content in English and another language, including Spanish.”.

2405 “Sec. 22a-1. Discontinuation of services under a Rapid Re-Housing program.
2406 “(a) Each client shall be exited from a Rapid Re-Housing program at the end of the time
2407 limit for services under the program. The time limit for assistance under the program shall be
2408 established by the Mayor by rule, but shall not be shorter than 12 months.
2409 “(b) The Mayor may extend a client’s time limit for services in a Rapid Re-Housing
2410 program beyond the time limit established pursuant to subsection (a) of this section, pursuant to
2411 subsection (e) of this section and procedures established by the Mayor by rule. If the Mayor
2412 extends a client’s time limit pursuant to this subsection, the client shall be exited from the Rapid
2413 Re-Housing program at the end of the extended time limit.
2414 “(c) The provision for continuation of services under section 22b(c)(1) shall not apply to
2415 a client who receives a notice of program exit from a Rapid Re-Housing program pursuant to
125

2416 subsection (a) or (b) of this section on or after the effective date of the Fiscal Year 2026 Budget
2417 Support Emergency Act of 2025.
2418 “(d)(1) A client who received a notice of program exit from a Rapid Re-Housing program
2419 before the effective date of the Fiscal Year 2026 Budget Support Emergency Act of 2025, when
2420 the exit was due to the end of a time limit for services to the client under the program, shall be
2421 exited from the Rapid Re-Housing program when the client’s time in the program reaches 24
2422 months or on September 30, 2025, whichever date is later.
2423 “(2) A program exit provided for in paragraph (1) of this subsection shall occur
2424 regardless of the pendency of an administrative review, fair hearing, or other appeal in which the
2425 client seeks to remain in the Rapid Re-Housing program beyond the client’s time limit for
2426 services and notwithstanding any statutory provision requiring the continuation of services that
2427 existed on or before the date the client received the notice of program exit.
2428 “(e)(1) A determination of whether to consider a request to extend a client’s time limit for
2429 services in a Rapid Re-Housing program need not be made on an individualized basis, and any
2430 determination of whether to consider or grant a request to extend a client’s time limit for services
2431 on the basis of the unavailability of funds shall be in the sole and absolute discretion of the
2432 Director of the Department.
2433 “(2) This subsection shall apply as of November 27, 2024.”.

2761 needs, clinician licensure levels, recruitment and retention challenges, the incorporation of non-
2762 licensed staff, professional development opportunities for Department and community-based
2763 organization clinicians, and an evaluation of the current staffing model, including the
2764 Department clinicians compared to clinicians employed through grant-funded partnerships with
2765 community-based organizations;
142

2766 “(6) An integration framework for behavioral-health and school-health services,
2767 developed in consultation with the Department of Health, to support collaboration between
2768 school-based behavioral-health clinicians and public-school and public-charter-school nurses;
2769 “(7) A review of performance metrics, curriculum standards, and quality
2770 assurance protocols for clinicians assigned to public and public charter schools, with proposed
2771 updates to strengthen accountability and service delivery outcomes;
2772 “(8) An assessment of the need for, and feasibility of, a common electronic health
2773 record platform or data-sharing interface between the Department and its contracted providers to
2774 support documentation, billing, and care coordination;
2775 “(9) A summary of input received from Department clinicians and community-
2776 based organization employed clinicians, including feedback on service-delivery challenges and
2777 recommendations for program improvement;
2778 “(10) A proposed structure and function for the program’s advisory council,
2779 including any changes to membership, scope, and meeting frequency to ensure the advisory
2780 council can effectively support implementation and accountability;
2781 “(11) A plan for how the Department will support the creation and maintenance of
2782 a comprehensive inventory of behavioral health resources in public and public charter schools,
2783 pursuant to section 4902b of the Department of Health Functions Clarifications Act of 2001,
2784 effective March 7, 2025 (D.C. Law 25-279; D.C. Official Code § 7-731.02), and the Healthy
2785 Schools Act of 2010, effective July 27, 2010 (D.C. Law 18-209; D.C. Official Code § 38-821.01
143

2786 et seq.), by partnering with school behavioral health coordinators to identify resource gaps and
2787 guide resource allocation and development; and

2797 outreach pilot.
2798 (a) By October 31, 2025, the Department Behavioral Health (“DBH”) shall award grants

2800 services to provide direct support, relationship development, and resource brokering to
2801 individuals in need of substance use and behavioral health services at the locations and in the
2802 amounts as follows:
2803 (1) $800,000 from the Opioid Abatement Fund, pursuant to section 5012(b-6)(1)
2804 of the Opioid Abatement Fund Establishment Act of 2022, effective September 21, 2022 (D.C.
2805 Law 24-167; D.C. Official Code § 7-3221(b-6)(1)), for:
2806 (A) The vicinity of the 600 block of T Street, NW;
144

2807 (B) The vicinity of the of the 1300-1700 blocks of North Capitol Street,
2808 NW, and 1600-1700 blocks of Lincoln Road, NE;
2809 (C) The vicinity of the 3800-4000 blocks of Minnesota Avenue, NE; and
2810 (D) The vicinity of the 1300-1800 blocks of Marion Barry Avenue, SE;
2811 and
2812 (2) $200,000 for the vicinity of the King Greenleaf Recreation Center, located at
2813 201 N Street, SW.
2814 (b) By October 31, 2025, DBH shall award a grant in the amount of $750,000 to an
2815 organization to provide direct support, relationship development and resource brokering to
2816 individuals at the following locations:
2817 (1) Columbia Heights Civic Plaza;
2818 (2) The intersection of Mount Pleasant Street, NW, and Kenyon Street, NW;
2819 (3) Georgia Avenue, NW, between New Hampshire Avenue, NW, and Harvard
2820 Street, NW; and
2821 (4) U Street, NW, between 14th Street, NW, and Georgia Avenue, NW.
2822 (c) By November 30, 2026, each not-for-profit organization awarded a grant pursuant to
2823 subsections (a) and (b) of this section (“grantee”) shall submit a report to DBH, which shall
2824 include the following information, broken down by location:
2825 (1) The number of individuals or groups the grantee engaged through outreach
2826 efforts;
145

2827 (2) The number of individuals the grantee connected to substance use disorder
2828 treatment programs, primary healthcare, mental health services, housing assistance, employment
2829 support, or other services;
2830 (3) The number of overdose reversals or interventions performed by the grantee
2831 using naloxone or other overdose reversal medications;
2832 (4) The amount of harm reduction supplies distributed by the grantee, including
2833 clean needles, syringes, naloxone kits, condoms, or other materials that reduce the risks
2834 associated with drug use; and
2835 (5) The number of educational sessions, workshops or prevention activities
2836 delivered by the grantee to target populations.
2837 (d) Within 30 days of receiving the report described in subsection (c) of this section,
2838 DBH shall submit the report to the Council and publicly post the report on its website.
2839 (e) For the locations specified in subsection (a) of this section, DBH shall award a grant
2840 to the same organizations that received grants to provide these services under the Department of
2841 Behavioral Health Targeted Outreach Grants Act of 2023, effective September 6, 2023 (D.C.
2842 Law 25-50; D.C. Official Code § 7-1141.01, note).

3112 Sec. 5232. Section 47-2853.76b of the District of Columbia Official Code is amended as
3113 follows:
3114 (a) Subsection (a) is amended as follows:

3115 (1) Strike the phrase “, through the Board of Barber and Cosmetology, shall

3119 its place.
3120 (3) Paragraph (1) is repealed.
3121 (4) Paragraph (2) is repealed.
3122 (b) New subsections (b), (c), and (d) are added to read as follows:
3123 “(b) The Department of Health shall regulate body art establishments to ensure that such
3124 establishments have adequate health, sanitization, sterilization and safety methods, procedures,
3125 equipment, and supplies by establishing minimum sterilization, sanitation, health, and safety
3126 standards for the operation of such establishments as may be necessary to prevent infection and
3127 contamination of equipment, supplies, or work surfaces with pathogenic organisms and by
3128 establishing and imposing operational licensing, registration requirements, and associated fee
3129 schedules.
3130 “(c)(1) All body art establishments offering tattooing procedures shall conspicuously post
3131 a written disclosure that states the following:
3132 “The United States Food and Drug Administration has not approved any pigment color
3133 additive for injectable use as tattoo ink. There may be a risk of carcinogenic decomposition
3134 associated with certain pigments when the pigments are subsequently exposed to concentrated
3135 ultra-violet light or laser irradiation.
160

3136 “(2) All body art establishments offering tattooing procedures shall maintain
3137 documentation on the premises containing the following information and shall disclose such
3138 information to customers upon request:
3139 “(A) The components of the pigments used in the body art establishment;
3140 “(B) The names, addresses, and telephone numbers of the suppliers and
3141 manufacturers of pigments used in the body art establishment for the past 3 years; and
3142 “(C) Identification of any recalled pigments used in the establishment for
3143 the past 3 years and the supplier and manufacturer of each pigment.
3144 “(3) All body art establishments shall maintain and use regularly calibrated
3145 autoclave equipment for the sterilization of any non-disposable body art equipment at a
3146 frequency to be established by the Department of Health.
3147 “(4) Only single-use disposable sharps, pigments, gloves, and cleansing products
3148 shall be used in connection with body art procedures in body art establishments, in accordance
3149 with rules established by the Department of Health pursuant to subsection (b) of this section.
3150 “(5) A body art establishment that is in violation of this subsection shall be
3151 subject to license suspension or revocation and a maximum fine of $2,500.
3152 “(d)(1) No person shall operate a body art establishment or perform body art procedures
3153 in a body art establishment unless that establishment has obtained a valid body art establishment
3154 license issued by the Mayor.
161

3155 “(2) No body art establishment shall employ or permit body artists to perform
3156 body art procedures in the body art establishment unless the body artist holds a valid body art
3157 license issued by the Mayor.
3158 “(3) Any person violating paragraph (1) or (2) of this subsection shall, upon
3159 conviction, be guilty of a misdemeanor and may be punished by a fine not exceeding $2,500,
3160 imprisonment for not more than 3 months, or both.”.

3605 Sec. 6121. Short title.
3606 This subtitle may be cited as the “Clean City Office Establishment Emergency
3607 Amendment Act of 2025”.
3608 Sec. 6122. Title I of the Sustainable Solid Waste Management Amendment Act of 2014,
3609 effective February 26, 2015 (D.C. Law 20-154; D.C. Official Code § 8-1031.01 et seq.), is
3610 amended by adding a new subtitle C to read as follows:
3611 “SUBTITLE C. Office of the Clean City.
3612 “Sec. 127. Establishment of the Office of the Clean City.
185

3613 “(a) There is established within the Department of Public Works the Office of the Clean
3614 City, which shall be headed by a full-time Clean City Coordinator, who shall be appointed by the
3615 Mayor.
3616 “(b) The Clean City Coordinator shall:
3617 “(1) Conduct cleanliness assessments on a quarterly basis for the entire District
3618 and on an as needed basis for the District of Columbia National Highway System and provide
3619 written reports and GIS maps documenting the outcomes of those assessments;
3620 “(2) Work in partnership and consultation with the various agencies and offices
3621 that have cleanliness and beautification operational responsibility to develop, coordinate and
3622 support Clean City program activities and to deliver Clean City services;
3623 “(3) Develop, coordinate and support Clean City program activities with agency
3624 divisions that have operational responsibility for maintaining the cleanliness of the District;
3625 “(4) Work with agency directors and staff to identify and resolve barriers to
3626 effective cooperation among multiple agencies to further the cleanliness of the District in areas
3627 including, but not limited to, financial, legal, or procurement services;
3628 “(5) Assist the Director of the Department of Public Works and the Office of
3629 Waste Diversion with innovations in public and household solid-waste container infrastructure
3630 and collections;
3631 “(6) Advocate for the enforcement of existing laws and municipal regulations that
3632 can have a positive impact on the cleanliness and appearance of the District;
186

3633 “(7) Solicit the involvement of ANCs, civic associations, concerned citizens, and
3634 businesses in litter-prevention programs and support for the cleaning of the District;
3635 “(8) Maintain a website containing information on Clean City activities,
3636 education, and community engagement information;
3637 “(9) Develop and support Clean City Initiative programs to educate and engage
3638 DC Public Schools and Public Charter School students in litter-prevention programs and support
3639 for the cleaning of the District;
3640 “(10) Formulate and implement a fundraising strategy to solicit corporate and
3641 foundation contributions towards Clean City Initiatives including “Adopt-A-Block” programs;
3642 “(11) Support the coordination of rodent-abatement programs between the
3643 Department of Public Works and Department of Health; and
3644 “(12) Support planning and resource allocation for pet-waste disposal.
3645 “(c) Subject to funding, the Clean City Coordinator may issue grants to support public-
3646 space cleaning efforts. Such grants shall:
3647 “(1) Preference supporting and expanding the service area of existing Clean
3648 Teams funded by the Department of Small and Local Business Development;
3649 “(2) Prioritize public space cleaning for major arterials, commercial corridors, and
3650 mixed-use neighborhoods; and
3651 “(3) Not be used to replace work performed by Department of Public Works
3652 staff.”.

4322 1978 (D.C. Law 2-103; D.C. Official Code § 42-2601 et seq.), is amended as follows:
4323 (a) Section 2 (D.C. Official Code § 42-2601), is amended to read as follows:
4324 “Sec. 2. Home Purchase Assistance Fund.
4325 “(a) There is established as a special fund the Home Purchase Assistance Fund (“Fund”),
4326 to be administered by the Mayor in accordance with subsection (c) of this section.
4327 “(b) The following revenue shall be deposited in the Fund:
4328 “(1) Such amounts as may be appropriated to the Fund;
4329 “(2) Grants and gifts from public and private sources to the Fund or to the District
4330 of Columbia for the purposes of the Fund;
4331 “(3) Repayments of principal and any interest on loans provided from the Fund;
4332 “(4) Proceeds realized from the liquidation of any security interests held by the
4333 District of Columbia under the terms of any assistance provided from the Fund;
4334 “(5) Interest earned from the deposit or investment of monies of the Fund;
4335 “(6) Repayments of principal and any interest on loans provided under the District
4336 of Columbia Government Employer-Assisted Housing Program; and
220

4337 “(7) All other revenues, receipts, and fees of whatever nature derived from the
4338 operation of the Fund.
4339 “(c)(1) Money in the Fund shall be used to provide financial assistance to low and
4340 moderate income persons, and District government employees participating in the District of
4341 Columbia Employer-Assisted Housing Program, and families seeking to purchase homes in the
4342 District of Columbia, for the purposes of enabling them to purchase decent, safe, and sanitary
4343 homes in the District of Columbia.
4344 “(2) Money in the Fund shall also be available for the purpose of providing
4345 financial assistance for down payments or interim financing to recipients for the purpose of
4346 purchasing or securing housing, including single family homes, condominium units, or
4347 occupancy rights to cooperative housing in the District of Columbia as their principal place of
4348 residence and of providing financial assistance to District of Columbia government employees
4349 eligible under the District of Columbia Employer-Assisted Housing Program to purchase a home
4350 in the District of Columbia.
4351 “(3) Under terms and conditions prescribed by the Mayor, the Fund may be used
4352 for making loans and providing other forms of financial assistance. The assistance provided
4353 pursuant to the Fund may be used in conjunction with other available home-assistance programs.
4354 “(d) Any money remaining available in the Fund at the end of a fiscal year, as determined
4355 by the Chief Financial Officer in the fiscal year-end close, shall be transferred to the unassigned
4356 fund balance of the General Fund of the District of Columbia as part of the fiscal year-end
4357 close.”.
221

4358 (b) Section 3 (D.C. Official Code § 42-2602) is repealed.

4709 “(2) There shall be deposited in the Fund any funds appropriated for the purposes

4852 Sec. 7172. Chapter 46 of Title 47 of the District of Columbia Official Code is amended as
4853 follows:
4854 (a) The table of contents is amended by adding a new section designation to read as
4855 follows:
4856 “47-4682. Tax Exemption for Reservoir District; Lots 809, 810, 814, 815, Square 3128.”.
4857 (b) A new section 47-4682 is added to read as follows:
4858 “§ 47-4682. Tax Exemption for Reservoir District; Lots 809, 810, 814, 815, Square 3128.
4859 “(a) For the purpose of this section, the term:
248

4860 “(1) “Owner” means McMillan Parcel 2 Owner, LLC, and McMillan Parcel 4
4861 Owner, LLC, affiliates of LDP Holdings, LLC d/b/a Jair Lynch Real Estate Partners, and its
4862 successors, affiliates, and assigns.
4863 “(2) “Property” means the real property, including any improvements constructed
4864 thereon, at Parcel 2 West and Parcel 4 within the Reservoir District; known for tax and
4865 assessment purposes as Lots 814 and 815 in Square 3128, and Lots 809 and 810 in Square 3128,
4866 respectively.
4867 “(b) Beginning on October 1, 2029, 100% of the real property tax imposed on the
4868 Property pursuant to Chapter 8 of this title shall be exempted for 20 real property tax years;
4869 provided, that the Owner shall:
4870 “(1) Operate or cause to be operated 449 units of housing at the Property;
4871 “(2) Set aside 1/3 of the operating rental housing units in the Property as
4872 affordable and available for households earning an average of 80% of the Area Median Income;
4873 “(3) Enter into an agreement with the District government that requires the
4874 Owner, or its designee or assignee, to, at a minimum, contract with certified business enterprises
4875 for at least 35% of the contract dollar volume of the construction of the project on the Property,
4876 in accordance with Subchapter IX-A of Chapter 2 of Title 2; and
4877 “(4) By September 30 of the year immediately preceding each tax year in the
4878 exemption period set forth in this subsection, provide the Mayor with information showing what
4879 percentage of each of the requirements for eligibility for the exemption provided in paragraphs
4880 (1) through (3) of this subsection has been met. If the total number of units of housing required
249

4881 to be provided pursuant to paragraph (1) of this subsection has not been met, the amount of the
4882 real property tax exemption shall be reduced in equal proportion to the percentage of units of
4883 housing that are not currently operating in the given real property tax year.
4884 “(c) By December 31 of each tax year of the exemption period provided in subsection (b)
4885 of this section, the Mayor shall certify to the Office of Tax and Revenue what percentage of tax
4886 exemption the Property is eligible to receive under this section for that tax year. The Mayor shall
4887 notify the Office of Tax and Revenue if the Property ceases to be eligible for the exemption and
4888 the date such eligibility ceased.
4889 “(d) The exemptions provided by this section shall be in addition to, and not in lieu of,
4890 any other tax relief or assistance from any other source applicable to the Owner or Property.”.

5060 adding a new subsection (e) to read as follows:
5061 “(e)(1) This section shall not apply to buildings or grounds used for solar energy
5062 generation, energy storage, solar energy management activities that comply with Energy Star
5063 guidelines, or electric vehicle charging.
5064 “(2) For the purpose of this subsection, the term:
5065 “(A) “Solar energy management activities” means activity intended to
5066 monitor, control, and optimize solar energy consumption to improve efficiency, reduce costs, and
5067 minimize environmental impacts.
258

5068 “(B) “Energy storage” means the collection and storage of energy
5069 generated by solar panels for later use, customarily through the use of battery energy storage
5070 systems.”.

5235 TITLE IX. APPLICABILITY; FISCAL IMPACT; EFFECTIVE DATE
5236 Sec. 9001. Applicability.
5237 Except as otherwise provided, this act shall apply as of October 1, 2025.
5238 Sec. 9002. Fiscal impact statement.
5239 The Council adopts the fiscal impact statement of the Chief Financial Officer as the fiscal
5240 impact statement required by section 4a of the General Legislative Procedures Act of 1975,
5241 approved October 16, 2006 (120 Stat. 2038; D.C. Official Code § 1-301.47a).
5242 Sec. 9003. Effective date.
5243 This act shall take effect following approval by the Mayor (or in the event of veto by the
5244 Mayor, action by the Council to override the veto), and shall remain in effect for no longer than
5245 90 days, as provided for emergency acts of the Council of the District of Columbia in section
5246 412(a) of the District of Columbia Home Rule Act, approved December 24, 1973 (87 Stat. 788;
5247 D.C. Official Code § 1-204.12(a)).
